	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Caribbean</h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
		<div id="contentSub"></div>
		
		
		
		<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>
		<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">This article is about the group of islands. For the indigenous inhabitants of Caribbean region and people of Caribbean descent, see <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_people" title="Caribbean people">Caribbean people</a>. For the body of water surrounding them, see <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">Caribbean Sea</a>. For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Caribbean (disambiguation)">Caribbean (disambiguation)</a>.</div>
<div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Region to the center-east of America composed of many islands / coastal regions surrounding the Caribbean Sea</div>

<p>The <b>Caribbean</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˌ/: secondary stress follows">ˌ</span><span title="&#39;k&#39; in &#39;kind&#39;">k</span><span title="/ær/: &#39;arr&#39; in &#39;marry&#39;">ær</span><span title="/ɪ/: &#39;i&#39; in &#39;kit&#39;">ɪ</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;b&#39; in &#39;buy&#39;">b</span><span title="/iː/: &#39;ee&#39; in &#39;fleece&#39;">iː</span><span title="/ə/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">ə</span><span title="&#39;n&#39; in &#39;nigh&#39;">n</span></span>, <wbr /><span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="&#39;k&#39; in &#39;kind&#39;">k</span><span title="/ə/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">ə</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;r&#39; in &#39;rye&#39;">r</span><span title="/ɪ/: &#39;i&#39; in &#39;kit&#39;">ɪ</span><span title="&#39;b&#39; in &#39;buy&#39;">b</span><span title="/i/: &#39;y&#39; in &#39;happy&#39;">i</span><span title="/ə/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">ə</span><span title="&#39;n&#39; in &#39;nigh&#39;">n</span></span>/</a></span></span>, <span class="nowrap"><small>locally </small><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;k&#39; in &#39;kind&#39;">k</span><span title="/ær/: &#39;arr&#39; in &#39;marry&#39;">ær</span><span title="/ɪ/: &#39;i&#39; in &#39;kit&#39;">ɪ</span><span title="&#39;b&#39; in &#39;buy&#39;">b</span><span title="/i/: &#39;y&#39; in &#39;happy&#39;">i</span><span title="/æ/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;bad&#39;">æ</span><span title="&#39;n&#39; in &#39;nigh&#39;">n</span></span>/</a></span></span>)<sup id="cite_ref-dce_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dce-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> is a region of <a href="/wiki/The_Americas" class="mw-redirect" title="The Americas">the Americas</a> that consists of the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">Caribbean Sea</a>, its islands (some surrounded by the Caribbean Sea<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> and some bordering both the Caribbean Sea and the North Atlantic Ocean)<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> and the surrounding coasts. The region is southeast of the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico" title="Gulf of Mexico">Gulf of Mexico</a> and the North American mainland, east of <a href="/wiki/Central_America" title="Central America">Central America</a>, and north of <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South America</a>.
</p><p>Situated largely on the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Plate" title="Caribbean Plate">Caribbean Plate</a>, the region has more than 700 islands, <a href="/wiki/Islet" title="Islet">islets</a>, <a href="/wiki/Reef" title="Reef">reefs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cay" title="Cay">cays</a> (see the <a href="/wiki/List_of_islands_in_the_Caribbean" class="mw-redirect" title="List of islands in the Caribbean">list of Caribbean islands</a>). <a href="/wiki/Island_arc" title="Island arc">Island arcs</a> delineate the eastern and northern edges of the Caribbean Sea:<sup id="cite_ref-brief_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-brief-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Greater_Antilles" title="Greater Antilles">Greater Antilles</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Lucayan_Archipelago" title="Lucayan Archipelago">Lucayan Archipelago</a> on the north and the <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Antilles" title="Lesser Antilles">Lesser Antilles</a> and the on the south and east (which includes the <a href="/wiki/Leeward_Antilles" title="Leeward Antilles">Leeward Antilles</a>).   The <a href="/wiki/Lucayan_Archipelago" title="Lucayan Archipelago">Lucayan Archipelago</a> (<a href="/wiki/The_Bahamas" title="The Bahamas">the Bahamas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Turks_and_Caicos_Islands" title="Turks and Caicos Islands">Turks and Caicos Islands</a>), do not border the Caribbean Sea, but are still within the boundaries of the Caribbean region. On the mainland, <a href="/wiki/Belize" title="Belize">Belize</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nicaragua" title="Nicaragua">Nicaragua</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_region_of_Colombia" title="Caribbean region of Colombia">Caribbean region of Colombia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cozumel" title="Cozumel">Cozumel</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Yucat%C3%A1n_Peninsula" title="Yucatán Peninsula">Yucatán Peninsula</a>, <a href="/wiki/Margarita_Island" title="Margarita Island">Margarita Island</a>, and <a href="/wiki/The_Guyanas" class="mw-redirect" title="The Guyanas">the Guyanas</a> (<a href="/wiki/Guyana" title="Guyana">Guyana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Suriname" title="Suriname">Suriname</a>, <a href="/wiki/French_Guiana" title="French Guiana">French Guiana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guayana_Region,_Venezuela" title="Guayana Region, Venezuela">Guayana Region in Venezuela</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Amap%C3%A1" title="Amapá">Amapá in Brazil</a>) are often included due to their <a href="/wiki/Political_geography" title="Political geography">political</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cultural_geography" title="Cultural geography">cultural</a> ties with the region.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Geopolitics" title="Geopolitics">Geopolitically</a>, the islands of the Caribbean (the <a href="/wiki/West_Indies" title="West Indies">West Indies</a>) are often regarded as a region of <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a>, though sometimes they are included in <a href="/wiki/Central_America" title="Central America">Central America</a> or left as a region of their own.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> and are organized into 30 territories including <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">sovereign states</a>, <a href="/wiki/Overseas_department_and_region" title="Overseas department and region">overseas departments</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Dependent_territory" title="Dependent territory">dependencies</a>. From December 15, 1954, to October 10, 2010, there was a country known as the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_Antilles" title="Netherlands Antilles">Netherlands Antilles</a> composed of five states, all of which were <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Dutch</a> dependencies.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>  From January 3, 1958, to May 31, 1962, there was also a short-lived political union called the <a href="/wiki/West_Indies_Federation" title="West Indies Federation">West Indies Federation</a> composed of ten <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a>-speaking Caribbean territories, all of which were then <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">British</a> dependencies. The <a href="/wiki/West_Indies_cricket_team" title="West Indies cricket team">West Indies cricket team</a> continues to represent many of those nations.
</p>
<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>
<ul>
<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#Etymology_and_pronunciation"><span class="tocnumber">1</span> <span class="toctext">Etymology and pronunciation</span></a></li>
<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-2"><a href="#Definition"><span class="tocnumber">2</span> <span class="toctext">Definition</span></a></li>
<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-3"><a href="#Geography_and_geology"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">Geography and geology</span></a>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_and_pronunciation">Etymology and pronunciation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caribbean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology and pronunciation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The region takes its name from that of the <a href="/wiki/Island_Caribs" title="Island Caribs">Caribs</a>, an ethnic group present in the <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Antilles" title="Lesser Antilles">Lesser Antilles</a> and parts of adjacent South America at the time of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="Spanish colonization of the Americas">Spanish conquest of the Americas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The two most prevalent pronunciations of "Caribbean" outside the Caribbean are <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˌ/: secondary stress follows">ˌ</span><span title="&#39;k&#39; in &#39;kind&#39;">k</span><span title="/ær/: &#39;arr&#39; in &#39;marry&#39;">ær</span><span title="/ɪ/: &#39;i&#39; in &#39;kit&#39;">ɪ</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;b&#39; in &#39;buy&#39;">b</span><span title="/iː/: &#39;ee&#39; in &#39;fleece&#39;">iː</span><span title="/ə/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">ə</span><span title="&#39;n&#39; in &#39;nigh&#39;">n</span></span>/</a></span></span> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i title="English pronunciation respelling"><span style="font-size:90%">KARR</span>-ə-<span style="font-size:90%">BEE</span>-ən</i></a>), with the primary stress on the third syllable, and <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="&#39;k&#39; in &#39;kind&#39;">k</span><span title="/ə/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">ə</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;r&#39; in &#39;rye&#39;">r</span><span title="/ɪ/: &#39;i&#39; in &#39;kit&#39;">ɪ</span><span title="&#39;b&#39; in &#39;buy&#39;">b</span><span title="/i/: &#39;y&#39; in &#39;happy&#39;">i</span><span title="/ə/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">ə</span><span title="&#39;n&#39; in &#39;nigh&#39;">n</span></span>/</a></span></span> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i title="English pronunciation respelling">kə-<span style="font-size:90%">RIB</span>-ee-ən</i></a>), with the stress on the second. Most authorities of the last century preferred the stress on the third syllable.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> This is the older of the two pronunciations, but the stressed-second-syllable variant has been established for over 75 years.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> It has been suggested that speakers of <a href="/wiki/British_English" title="British English">British English</a> prefer <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˌ/: secondary stress follows">ˌ</span><span title="&#39;k&#39; in &#39;kind&#39;">k</span><span title="/ær/: &#39;arr&#39; in &#39;marry&#39;">ær</span><span title="/ɪ/: &#39;i&#39; in &#39;kit&#39;">ɪ</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;b&#39; in &#39;buy&#39;">b</span><span title="/iː/: &#39;ee&#39; in &#39;fleece&#39;">iː</span><span title="/ə/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">ə</span><span title="&#39;n&#39; in &#39;nigh&#39;">n</span></span>/</a></span></span> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i title="English pronunciation respelling"><span style="font-size:90%">KARR</span>-ə-<span style="font-size:90%">BEE</span>-ən</i></a>) while North American speakers more typically use <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="&#39;k&#39; in &#39;kind&#39;">k</span><span title="/ə/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">ə</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;r&#39; in &#39;rye&#39;">r</span><span title="/ɪ/: &#39;i&#39; in &#39;kit&#39;">ɪ</span><span title="&#39;b&#39; in &#39;buy&#39;">b</span><span title="/i/: &#39;y&#39; in &#39;happy&#39;">i</span><span title="/ə/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">ə</span><span title="&#39;n&#39; in &#39;nigh&#39;">n</span></span>/</a></span></span> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i title="English pronunciation respelling">kə-<span style="font-size:90%">RIB</span>-ee-ən</i></a>),<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> but major American dictionaries and other sources list the stress on the third syllable as more common in <a href="/wiki/American_English" title="American English">American English</a> too.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> According to the American version of Oxford Online Dictionaries, the stress on the second syllable is becoming more common in UK English and is increasingly considered "by some" to be more up to date and more "correct".<sup id="cite_ref-oed_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oed-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Oxford Online Dictionaries claim that the stress on the second syllable is the most common pronunciation in the Caribbean itself, but according to the Dictionary of Caribbean English Usage, the most common pronunciation in <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_English" title="Caribbean English">Caribbean English</a> stresses the first syllable instead, <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;k&#39; in &#39;kind&#39;">k</span><span title="/ær/: &#39;arr&#39; in &#39;marry&#39;">ær</span><span title="/ɪ/: &#39;i&#39; in &#39;kit&#39;">ɪ</span><span title="&#39;b&#39; in &#39;buy&#39;">b</span><span title="/i/: &#39;y&#39; in &#39;happy&#39;">i</span><span title="/æ/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;bad&#39;">æ</span><span title="&#39;n&#39; in &#39;nigh&#39;">n</span></span>/</a></span></span> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i title="English pronunciation respelling"><span style="font-size:90%">KARR</span>-ih-bee-an</i></a>).<sup id="cite_ref-dce_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dce-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-oed_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oed-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Definition">Definition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caribbean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Definition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:CIA_map_of_the_Caribbean.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/CIA_map_of_the_Caribbean.png/300px-CIA_map_of_the_Caribbean.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="207" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/CIA_map_of_the_Caribbean.png/450px-CIA_map_of_the_Caribbean.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/CIA_map_of_the_Caribbean.png/600px-CIA_map_of_the_Caribbean.png 2x" data-file-width="1291" data-file-height="892" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:CIA_map_of_the_Caribbean.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of the Caribbean</div></div></div>
<p>The word "Caribbean" has multiple uses. Its principal ones are geographical and political. The Caribbean can also be expanded to include territories with strong cultural and historical connections to Africa, <a href="/wiki/Slavery" title="Slavery">slavery</a>, <a href="/wiki/European_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="European colonization of the Americas">European colonisation</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Plantation_system" class="mw-redirect" title="Plantation system">plantation system</a>.
</p>
<ul><li>The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_geoscheme_for_the_Americas" title="United Nations geoscheme for the Americas">United Nations geoscheme for the Americas</a> presents the Caribbean as a distinct region within the <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">Americas</a>.</li>
<li>Physiographically, the Caribbean region is mainly a chain of islands surrounding the Caribbean Sea. To the north, the region is bordered by the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico" title="Gulf of Mexico">Gulf of Mexico</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Straits_of_Florida" title="Straits of Florida">Straits of Florida</a> and the Northern <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a>, which lies to the east and northeast. To the south lies the coastline of the continent of <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South America</a>.</li>
<li>Politically, the "Caribbean" may be centred by considering narrower and wider <a href="/wiki/Socio-economic" class="mw-redirect" title="Socio-economic">socio-economic</a> groupings:
<ul><li>At its core is the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Community" title="Caribbean Community">Caribbean Community</a> (CARICOM), whose full members include the <a href="/wiki/Bahamas" class="mw-redirect" title="Bahamas">Commonwealth of the Bahamas</a> in the Atlantic, the <a href="/wiki/Guyana" title="Guyana">Co-operative Republic of Guyana</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Suriname" title="Suriname">Republic of Suriname</a> in South America, and <a href="/wiki/Belize" title="Belize">Belize</a> in Central America; its associate members include <a href="/wiki/Bermuda" title="Bermuda">Bermuda</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Turks_and_Caicos_Islands" title="Turks and Caicos Islands">Turks and Caicos Islands</a> in the Atlantic Ocean.</li>
<li>Most expansive is the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Caribbean_States" title="Association of Caribbean States">Association of Caribbean States</a> (ACS), which includes almost every nation in the region surrounding the Caribbean and also <a href="/wiki/El_Salvador" title="El Salvador">El Salvador</a> on the Pacific Ocean. According to the ACS, the total population of its member states is 227 million people.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup></li></ul></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography_and_geology">Geography and geology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caribbean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Geography and geology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tectonic_plates_Caribbean.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Tectonic_plates_Caribbean.png/220px-Tectonic_plates_Caribbean.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Tectonic_plates_Caribbean.png/330px-Tectonic_plates_Caribbean.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Tectonic_plates_Caribbean.png/440px-Tectonic_plates_Caribbean.png 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tectonic_plates_Caribbean.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #FAD4AF; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;The <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Plate" title="Caribbean Plate">Caribbean Plate</a></div></div></div></div>
<p>The geography and climate in the Caribbean region varies: Some islands in the region have relatively flat terrain of non-volcanic origin. These islands include <a href="/wiki/Aruba" title="Aruba">Aruba</a> (possessing only minor volcanic features), <a href="/wiki/Cura%C3%A7ao" title="Curaçao">Curaçao</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">Barbados</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bonaire" title="Bonaire">Bonaire</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Cayman_Islands" title="Cayman Islands">Cayman Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Croix" title="Saint Croix">Saint Croix</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Bahamas" title="The Bahamas">the Bahamas</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Antigua" title="Antigua">Antigua</a>. Others possess rugged towering mountain-ranges like the islands of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Martin" title="Saint Martin">Saint Martin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hispaniola" title="Hispaniola">Hispaniola</a>, <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">Jamaica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dominica" title="Dominica">Dominica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Montserrat" title="Montserrat">Montserrat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saba" title="Saba">Saba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sint_Eustatius" title="Sint Eustatius">Sint Eustatius</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Kitts" title="Saint Kitts">Saint Kitts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Lucia" title="Saint Lucia">Saint Lucia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Thomas,_U.S._Virgin_Islands" title="Saint Thomas, U.S. Virgin Islands">Saint Thomas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_John,_U.S._Virgin_Islands" title="Saint John, U.S. Virgin Islands">Saint John</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tortola" title="Tortola">Tortola</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grenada" title="Grenada">Grenada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Vincent_(Antilles)" title="Saint Vincent (Antilles)">Saint Vincent</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guadeloupe" title="Guadeloupe">Guadeloupe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Martinique" title="Martinique">Martinique</a> and <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Trinidad and Tobago">Trinidad and Tobago</a>.
</p><p>Definitions of the terms Greater Antilles and Lesser Antilles often vary. The Virgin Islands as part of the Puerto Rican bank are sometimes included with the Greater Antilles. The term Lesser Antilles is often used to define an island arc that includes Grenada but excludes Trinidad and Tobago and the Leeward Antilles.
</p><p>The waters of the Caribbean Sea host large, migratory schools of fish, turtles, and <a href="/wiki/Coral_reef" title="Coral reef">coral reef</a> formations. The <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Trench" title="Puerto Rico Trench">Puerto Rico Trench</a>, located on the fringe of the Atlantic Ocean and Caribbean Sea just to the north of the island of Puerto Rico, is the deepest point in all of the Atlantic Ocean.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The region sits in the line of several major shipping routes with the <a href="/wiki/Panama_Canal" title="Panama Canal">Panama Canal</a> connecting the western Caribbean Sea with the Pacific Ocean.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caribbean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Johny_Cay.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Johny_Cay.jpg/220px-Johny_Cay.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Johny_Cay.jpg/330px-Johny_Cay.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Johny_Cay.jpg/440px-Johny_Cay.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4019" data-file-height="2674" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Johny_Cay.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Tropical monsoon climate in <a href="/wiki/San_Andr%C3%A9s_(island)" title="San Andrés (island)">San Andrés island</a>, Caribbean, <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a>.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_Caribbean_present.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Koppen-Geiger_Map_Caribbean_present.svg/220px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_Caribbean_present.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="116" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Koppen-Geiger_Map_Caribbean_present.svg/330px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_Caribbean_present.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Koppen-Geiger_Map_Caribbean_present.svg/440px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_Caribbean_present.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1609" data-file-height="850" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_Caribbean_present.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate</a> map of the islands of the Caribbean.</div></div></div>
<p>The climate of the area is <a href="/wiki/Tropical" class="mw-redirect" title="Tropical">tropical</a>, varying from <a href="/wiki/Tropical_rainforest_climate" title="Tropical rainforest climate">tropical rainforest</a> in some areas to <a href="/wiki/Tropical_monsoon_climate" title="Tropical monsoon climate">tropical monsoon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tropical_savanna_climate" title="Tropical savanna climate">tropical savanna</a> in others. There are also some locations that are <a href="/wiki/Arid" title="Arid">arid</a> climates with considerable drought in some years, and the peaks of mountains tend to have cooler <a href="/wiki/Temperate_climate" title="Temperate climate">temperate climates</a>.
</p><p>Rainfall varies with elevation, size and water currents, such as the cool upwellings that keep the <a href="/wiki/ABC_islands_(Lesser_Antilles)" title="ABC islands (Lesser Antilles)">ABC islands</a> arid. Warm, moist <a href="/wiki/Trade_winds" title="Trade winds">trade winds</a> blow consistently from the east, creating both rain forest and semi arid climates across the region. The tropical rainforest climates include lowland areas near the Caribbean Sea from <a href="/wiki/Costa_Rica" title="Costa Rica">Costa Rica</a> north to <a href="/wiki/Belize" title="Belize">Belize</a>, as well as the <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominican Republic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a>, while the more seasonal dry tropical savanna climates are found in <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>, northern  <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a>, and southern <a href="/wiki/Yucat%C3%A1n_Peninsula" title="Yucatán Peninsula">Yucatán, Mexico</a>. Arid climates are found along the extreme northern coast of Venezuela out to the islands including <a href="/wiki/Aruba" title="Aruba">Aruba</a> and <a href="/wiki/Curacao" class="mw-redirect" title="Curacao">Curacao</a>, as well as the northwestern tip of Yucatán.
</p><p>While the region generally is sunny much of the year, the wet season from May through November sees more frequent cloud cover (both broken and overcast), while the dry season from December through April is more often clear to mostly sunny. Seasonal rainfall is divided into 'dry' and 'wet' seasons, with the latter six months of the year being wetter than the first half. The air temperature is hot much of the year, varying from 25 to 33 C (77 F to 90 F) between the wet and dry seasons. Seasonally, monthly mean temperatures vary from only about 5 C (7 F) in the northern most regions, to less than 3 C  in the southernmost areas of the Caribbean.
</p><p>Hurricane season is from June to November, but they occur more frequently in August and September and more common in the northern islands of the Caribbean. <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone#Hurricane_or_typhoon" title="Tropical cyclone">Hurricanes</a> that sometimes batter the region usually strike northwards of <a href="/wiki/Grenada" title="Grenada">Grenada</a> and to the west of Barbados. The principal hurricane belt arcs to northwest of the island of Barbados in the Eastern Caribbean. A great example being recent events of Hurricane Irma devastating the island of Saint Martin during the 2017 hurricane season.
</p><p>Sea surface temperatures change little annually, normally running from 30&#160;°C (87&#160;°F) in the warmest months to 26&#160;°C (76&#160;°F) in the coolest months. The air temperature is warm year round, in the 70s, 80s and 90s, and only varies from winter to summer about 2–5 degrees on the southern islands and about a 10–20 degrees difference on the northern islands of the Caribbean. The northern islands, like the Bahamas, Cuba, Puerto Rico and the Dominican Republic, may be influenced by continental masses during winter months, such as cold fronts.
</p><p><b>Aruba: Latitude 12°N</b>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Historical_groupings">Historical groupings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caribbean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Historical groupings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Caribbean" title="History of the Caribbean">History of the Caribbean</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Spanish_Caribbean_Islands_in_the_American_Viceroyalties_1600.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Spanish_Caribbean_Islands_in_the_American_Viceroyalties_1600.png/300px-Spanish_Caribbean_Islands_in_the_American_Viceroyalties_1600.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="179" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Spanish_Caribbean_Islands_in_the_American_Viceroyalties_1600.png/450px-Spanish_Caribbean_Islands_in_the_American_Viceroyalties_1600.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Spanish_Caribbean_Islands_in_the_American_Viceroyalties_1600.png/600px-Spanish_Caribbean_Islands_in_the_American_Viceroyalties_1600.png 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="953" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Spanish_Caribbean_Islands_in_the_American_Viceroyalties_1600.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Spanish Caribbean Islands in the American Viceroyalties 1600</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Political_Evolution_of_Central_America_and_the_Caribbean_1700_and_on.gif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Political_Evolution_of_Central_America_and_the_Caribbean_1700_and_on.gif/220px-Political_Evolution_of_Central_America_and_the_Caribbean_1700_and_on.gif" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Political_Evolution_of_Central_America_and_the_Caribbean_1700_and_on.gif/330px-Political_Evolution_of_Central_America_and_the_Caribbean_1700_and_on.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Political_Evolution_of_Central_America_and_the_Caribbean_1700_and_on.gif/440px-Political_Evolution_of_Central_America_and_the_Caribbean_1700_and_on.gif 2x" data-file-width="850" data-file-height="638" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Political_Evolution_of_Central_America_and_the_Caribbean_1700_and_on.gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Political evolution of Central America and the Caribbean from 1700 to present</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Caribbean_spanish_names.PNG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Caribbean_spanish_names.PNG/220px-Caribbean_spanish_names.PNG" decoding="async" width="220" height="128" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Caribbean_spanish_names.PNG/330px-Caribbean_spanish_names.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Caribbean_spanish_names.PNG/440px-Caribbean_spanish_names.PNG 2x" data-file-width="1861" data-file-height="1085" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Caribbean_spanish_names.PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The mostly Spanish-controlled Caribbean in the 16th century</div></div></div>
<p>All islands at some point were, and a few still are, <a href="/wiki/Colony" title="Colony">colonies</a> of European nations; a few are <a href="/wiki/Dependent_territory" title="Dependent territory">overseas or dependent territories</a>:
</p>
<ul><li><b><a href="/wiki/British_West_Indies" title="British West Indies">British West Indies</a>/<a href="/wiki/Anglophone_Caribbean" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglophone Caribbean">Anglophone Caribbean</a></b> – <a href="/wiki/Anguilla" title="Anguilla">Anguilla</a>, <a href="/wiki/Antigua_and_Barbuda" title="Antigua and Barbuda">Antigua and Barbuda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bahamas" class="mw-redirect" title="Bahamas">Bahamas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">Barbados</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bay_Islands_Department" title="Bay Islands Department">Bay Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guyana" title="Guyana">Guyana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Belize" title="Belize">Belize</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_Virgin_Islands" title="British Virgin Islands">British Virgin Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cayman_Islands" title="Cayman Islands">Cayman Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dominica" title="Dominica">Dominica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grenada" title="Grenada">Grenada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">Jamaica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Montserrat" title="Montserrat">Montserrat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Croix" title="Saint Croix">Saint Croix</a> (briefly), <a href="/wiki/Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis" title="Saint Kitts and Nevis">Saint Kitts and Nevis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Lucia" title="Saint Lucia">Saint Lucia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines" title="Saint Vincent and the Grenadines">Saint Vincent and the Grenadines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Trinidad and Tobago">Trinidad and Tobago</a> (from 1797) and the <a href="/wiki/Turks_and_Caicos_Islands" title="Turks and Caicos Islands">Turks and Caicos Islands</a></li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Danish_West_Indies" title="Danish West Indies">Danish West Indies</a></b> – Possession of <a href="/wiki/Denmark-Norway" class="mw-redirect" title="Denmark-Norway">Denmark-Norway</a> before <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_Constitution" class="mw-redirect" title="Norwegian Constitution">1814</a>, then <a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark">Denmark</a>, present-day <a href="/wiki/United_States_Virgin_Islands" title="United States Virgin Islands">United States Virgin Islands</a></li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Dutch_West_Indies" class="mw-redirect" title="Dutch West Indies">Dutch West Indies</a></b> – <a href="/wiki/Aruba" title="Aruba">Aruba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bonaire" title="Bonaire">Bonaire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cura%C3%A7ao" title="Curaçao">Curaçao</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saba" title="Saba">Saba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sint_Eustatius" title="Sint Eustatius">Sint Eustatius</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sint_Maarten" title="Sint Maarten">Sint Maarten</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bay_Islands_Department" title="Bay Islands Department">Bay Islands</a> (briefly), <a href="/wiki/Saint_Croix" title="Saint Croix">Saint Croix</a> (briefly), <a href="/wiki/Tobago" title="Tobago">Tobago</a>, <a href="/wiki/Suriname" title="Suriname">Surinam</a> and <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Islands" title="Virgin Islands">Virgin Islands</a></li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/French_West_Indies" title="French West Indies">French West Indies</a></b> – <a href="/wiki/Anguilla" title="Anguilla">Anguilla</a> (briefly), <a href="/wiki/Antigua_and_Barbuda" title="Antigua and Barbuda">Antigua and Barbuda</a> (briefly), <a href="/wiki/Dominica" title="Dominica">Dominica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominican Republic</a> (briefly), <a href="/wiki/Grenada" title="Grenada">Grenada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haiti</a> (formerly <a href="/wiki/Saint-Domingue" title="Saint-Domingue">Saint-Domingue</a>), <a href="/wiki/Montserrat" title="Montserrat">Montserrat</a> (briefly), <a href="/wiki/Saint_Lucia" title="Saint Lucia">Saint Lucia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines" title="Saint Vincent and the Grenadines">Saint Vincent and the Grenadines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sint_Eustatius" title="Sint Eustatius">Sint Eustatius</a> (briefly), <a href="/wiki/Sint_Maarten" title="Sint Maarten">Sint Maarten</a>, <a href="/wiki/St._Kitts" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Kitts">St. Kitts</a> (briefly), <a href="/wiki/Tobago" title="Tobago">Tobago</a> (briefly), <a href="/wiki/Saint_Croix" title="Saint Croix">Saint Croix</a>, the current French <a href="/wiki/D%C3%A9partement_d%27outre-mer" class="mw-redirect" title="Département d&#39;outre-mer">overseas <i>départements</i></a> of <a href="/wiki/French_Guiana" title="French Guiana">French Guiana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Martinique" title="Martinique">Martinique</a> and <a href="/wiki/Guadeloupe" title="Guadeloupe">Guadeloupe</a> (including <a href="/wiki/Marie-Galante" title="Marie-Galante">Marie-Galante</a>, <a href="/wiki/La_D%C3%A9sirade" title="La Désirade">La Désirade</a> and <a href="/wiki/Les_Saintes" class="mw-redirect" title="Les Saintes">Les Saintes</a>), the current French <a href="/wiki/Collectivit%C3%A9_d%27outre-mer" class="mw-redirect" title="Collectivité d&#39;outre-mer">overseas collectivities</a> of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Barth%C3%A9lemy" title="Saint Barthélemy">Saint Barthélemy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Collectivity_of_Saint_Martin" title="Collectivity of Saint Martin">Saint Martin</a></li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portuguese West Indies</a></b> – present-day <a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">Barbados</a>, known as <i><i lang="pt" title="Portuguese language text">Os Barbados</i></i> in the 16th century when the Portuguese claimed the island en route to Brazil. The Portuguese left Barbados abandoned years before the British arrived.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Spanish_West_Indies" title="Spanish West Indies">Spanish West Indies</a></b> – <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hispaniola" title="Hispaniola">Hispaniola</a> (present-day <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominican Republic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haiti</a> (until 1659 to France), <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">Jamaica</a> (until 1655 to Great Britain), the <a href="/wiki/Cayman_Islands" title="Cayman Islands">Cayman Islands</a> (until 1670 to Great Britain) <a href="/wiki/Trinidad" title="Trinidad">Trinidad</a> (until 1797 to Great Britain) and <a href="/wiki/Bay_Islands_Department" title="Bay Islands Department">Bay Islands</a> (until 1643 to Great Britain), coastal islands of <a href="/wiki/Central_America" title="Central America">Central America</a> (except Belize), and some Caribbean coastal islands of <a href="/wiki/Panama" title="Panama">Panama</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a>.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Swedish_West_Indies" class="mw-redirect" title="Swedish West Indies">Swedish West Indies</a></b> – present-day French <a href="/wiki/Saint-Barth%C3%A9lemy" class="mw-redirect" title="Saint-Barthélemy">Saint-Barthélemy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guadeloupe" title="Guadeloupe">Guadeloupe</a> (briefly) and <a href="/wiki/Tobago" title="Tobago">Tobago</a> (briefly).</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Courland_colonization_of_the_Americas" class="mw-redirect" title="Courland colonization of the Americas">Courlander West Indies</a></b> – <a href="/wiki/Tobago" title="Tobago">Tobago</a> (until 1691)</li></ul>
<p>The British West Indies were united by the United Kingdom into a <a href="/wiki/West_Indies_Federation" title="West Indies Federation">West Indies Federation</a> between 1958 and 1962. The independent countries formerly part of the B.W.I. still have a joint <a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">cricket</a> team that competes in <a href="/wiki/Test_cricket" title="Test cricket">Test matches</a>, <a href="/wiki/One_Day_International" title="One Day International">One Day Internationals</a> and <a href="/wiki/Twenty20_International" title="Twenty20 International">Twenty20 Internationals</a>. The <a href="/wiki/West_Indian_cricket_team" class="mw-redirect" title="West Indian cricket team">West Indian cricket team</a> includes the South American nation of <a href="/wiki/Guyana" title="Guyana">Guyana</a>, the only former British colony on the mainland of that continent.
</p><p>In addition, these countries share the <a href="/wiki/University_of_the_West_Indies" title="University of the West Indies">University of the West Indies</a> as a regional entity. The university consists of three main campuses in Jamaica, Barbados and Trinidad and Tobago, a smaller campus in the Bahamas and Resident Tutors in other contributing territories such as Trinidad.
</p>

<li><a href="/wiki/Patos_Island_(Venezuela)" title="Patos Island (Venezuela)">Patos Island</a></li></ul></li></ul>
<p>&#32;
</p>
</td></tr></tbody></table></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Biodiversity">Biodiversity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caribbean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Biodiversity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The Caribbean islands have one of the most diverse eco systems in the world. The animals, fungi and plants, and have been classified as one of <a href="/wiki/Conservation_International" title="Conservation International">Conservation International</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity_hotspot" title="Biodiversity hotspot">biodiversity hotspots</a> because of their exceptionally diverse terrestrial and marine ecosystems, ranging from montane <a href="/wiki/Cloud_forests" class="mw-redirect" title="Cloud forests">cloud forests</a>, to <a href="/wiki/Tropical_rainforest" title="Tropical rainforest">tropical rainforest</a>,  to <a href="/wiki/Cactus" title="Cactus">cactus</a> <a href="/wiki/Scrubland" class="mw-redirect" title="Scrubland">scrublands</a>. The region also contains about 8% (by surface area) of the world's coral reefs<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> along with extensive seagrass meadows,<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> both of which are frequently found in the shallow marine waters bordering the island and continental coasts of the region.
</p><p>For the fungi, there is a modern checklist based on nearly 90,000 records derived from specimens in reference collections, published accounts and field observations.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> That checklist includes more than 11,250 species of fungi recorded from the region. As its authors note, the work is far from exhaustive, and it is likely that the true total number of fungal species already known from the Caribbean is higher. The true total number of fungal species occurring in the Caribbean, including species not yet recorded, is likely far higher given the generally accepted estimate that only about 7% of all fungi worldwide have been discovered.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> Though the amount of available information is still small, a first effort has been made to estimate the number of fungal species endemic to some Caribbean islands. For Cuba, 2200 species of fungi have been tentatively identified as possible endemics of the island;<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> for <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a>, the number is 789 species;<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> for the <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominican Republic</a>, the number is 699 species;<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> for Trinidad and Tobago, the number is 407 species.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Many of the <a href="/wiki/Ecosystem" title="Ecosystem">ecosystems</a> of the Caribbean islands have been devastated by <a href="/wiki/Deforestation" title="Deforestation">deforestation</a>, pollution, and human encroachment. The arrival of the first humans is correlated with extinction of <a href="/wiki/Tyto_pollens" title="Tyto pollens">giant</a> <a href="/wiki/Ornimegalonyx" title="Ornimegalonyx">owls</a> and <a href="/wiki/Megalocnus" title="Megalocnus">dwarf ground sloths</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> The hotspot contains dozens of highly threatened animals (ranging from birds, to mammals and reptiles), fungi and plants. Examples of threatened animals include the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rican_amazon" title="Puerto Rican amazon">Puerto Rican amazon</a>, two species of <a href="/wiki/Solenodon" title="Solenodon">solenodon</a> (giant shrews) in Cuba and the Hispaniola island, and the <a href="/wiki/Cuban_crocodile" title="Cuban crocodile">Cuban crocodile</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin:0 auto;overflow:hidden;width:auto;max-width:758px"><div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize" style="overflow:auto"><a href="/wiki/File:Isla_Saona.jpg" class="image" title="Saona Island, Dominican Republic"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Isla_Saona.jpg/750px-Isla_Saona.jpg" decoding="async" width="750" height="159" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Isla_Saona.jpg/1125px-Isla_Saona.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Isla_Saona.jpg/1500px-Isla_Saona.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3173" data-file-height="674" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="text-align:center"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Isla_Saona.jpg" title="File:Isla Saona.jpg"> </a></div><a href="/wiki/Saona_Island" title="Saona Island">Saona Island</a>, Dominican Republic</div></div></div>
<p>The region's coral reefs, which contain about 70 species of hard corals and between 500–700 species of reef-associated fishes<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> have undergone rapid decline in ecosystem integrity in recent years, and are considered particularly vulnerable to global warming and ocean acidification.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> According to a <a href="/wiki/UNEP" class="mw-redirect" title="UNEP">UNEP</a> report, the Caribbean coral reefs might get extinct in next 20 years due to population explosion along the coast lines, overfishing, the pollution of coastal areas and global warming.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Some Caribbean islands have terrain that Europeans found suitable for cultivation for agriculture. <a href="/wiki/Tobacco" title="Tobacco">Tobacco</a> was an important early crop during the colonial era, but was eventually overtaken by <a href="/wiki/Sugarcane" title="Sugarcane">sugarcane</a> production as the region's staple crop. Sugar was produced from sugarcane for export to Europe. <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a> and <a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">Barbados</a> were historically the largest producers of <a href="/wiki/Sugar" title="Sugar">sugar</a>. The tropical plantation system thus came to dominate Caribbean settlement.  Other islands were found to have terrain unsuited for <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">agriculture</a>, for example <a href="/wiki/Dominica" title="Dominica">Dominica</a>, which remains heavily forested. The islands in the southern <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Antilles" title="Lesser Antilles">Lesser Antilles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aruba" title="Aruba">Aruba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bonaire" title="Bonaire">Bonaire</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cura%C3%A7ao" title="Curaçao">Curaçao</a>, are extremely arid, making them unsuitable for agriculture. However, they have <a href="/wiki/Salt" title="Salt">salt</a> pans that were exploited by the Dutch. Sea water was pumped into shallow ponds, producing coarse salt when the water evaporated.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The natural environmental diversity of the Caribbean islands has led to recent growth in <a href="/wiki/Eco-tourism" class="mw-redirect" title="Eco-tourism">eco-tourism</a>. This type of tourism is growing on islands lacking sandy beaches and dense human populations.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Plants_and_animals">Plants and animals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caribbean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Plants and animals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caribbean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Indigenous_groups">Indigenous groups</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caribbean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Indigenous groups">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Arawak_peoples" class="mw-redirect" title="Arawak peoples">Arawak peoples</a>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Igneri" title="Igneri">Igneri</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Taíno people">Taíno</a></li></ul></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Caquetio_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Caquetio people">Caquetio people</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ciboney" title="Ciboney">Ciboney</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Neo-Ta%C3%ADno_nations#Ciguayo" class="mw-redirect" title="Neo-Taíno nations">Ciguayo</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Garifuna_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Garifuna people">Garifuna</a></li>

<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:East_Indian_Coolies_in_Trinidad_-_Project_Gutenberg_eText_16035.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/East_Indian_Coolies_in_Trinidad_-_Project_Gutenberg_eText_16035.jpg/220px-East_Indian_Coolies_in_Trinidad_-_Project_Gutenberg_eText_16035.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="136" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/East_Indian_Coolies_in_Trinidad_-_Project_Gutenberg_eText_16035.jpg/330px-East_Indian_Coolies_in_Trinidad_-_Project_Gutenberg_eText_16035.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/East_Indian_Coolies_in_Trinidad_-_Project_Gutenberg_eText_16035.jpg/440px-East_Indian_Coolies_in_Trinidad_-_Project_Gutenberg_eText_16035.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1621" data-file-height="1000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:East_Indian_Coolies_in_Trinidad_-_Project_Gutenberg_eText_16035.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Indo-Trinidadian_and_Tobagonian" title="Indo-Trinidadian and Tobagonian">Asian Indians</a> in the late nineteenth century singing and dancing in <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Trinidad and Tobago">Trinidad and Tobago</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Scenes_of_Cuba_(K5_02567)_(5981599576).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Scenes_of_Cuba_%28K5_02567%29_%285981599576%29.jpg/220px-Scenes_of_Cuba_%28K5_02567%29_%285981599576%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Scenes_of_Cuba_%28K5_02567%29_%285981599576%29.jpg/330px-Scenes_of_Cuba_%28K5_02567%29_%285981599576%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Scenes_of_Cuba_%28K5_02567%29_%285981599576%29.jpg/440px-Scenes_of_Cuba_%28K5_02567%29_%285981599576%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4928" data-file-height="3264" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Scenes_of_Cuba_(K5_02567)_(5981599576).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Street scene, <a href="/wiki/Matanzas" title="Matanzas">Matanzas</a>, Cuba</div></div></div>
<p>At the time of <a href="/wiki/European_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="European colonization of the Americas">European contact</a>, the dominant ethnic groups in the Caribbean included the <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno" title="Taíno">Taíno</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Greater_Antilles" title="Greater Antilles">Greater Antilles</a> and northern <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Antilles" title="Lesser Antilles">Lesser Antilles</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Island_Caribs" title="Island Caribs">Island Caribs</a> of the southern Lesser Antilles, and smaller distinct groups such as the <a href="/wiki/Guanajatabey" class="mw-redirect" title="Guanajatabey">Guanajatabey</a> of western Cuba and the <a href="/wiki/Ciguayo" class="mw-redirect" title="Ciguayo">Ciguayo</a> of eastern Hispaniola. The population of the Caribbean is estimated to have been around 750,000 immediately before European contact, although lower and higher figures are given. After contact, social disruption and epidemic diseases such as smallpox and measles (to which they had no natural immunity)<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> led to a decline in the Amerindian population.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> From 1500 to 1800 the population rose as slaves arrived from West Africa<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> such as the <a href="/wiki/Kongo_people" title="Kongo people">Kongo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Igbo_people" title="Igbo people">Igbo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Akan_people" title="Akan people">Akan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fon_people" title="Fon people">Fon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yoruba_people" title="Yoruba people">Yoruba</a> as well as military prisoners from <a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland">Ireland</a>, who were deported during the Cromwellian reign in <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Immigrants from <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain" title="Great Britain">Britain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark">Denmark</a> also arrived, although the mortality rate was high for both groups.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The population is estimated to have reached 2.2 million by 1800.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> Immigrants from <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>, <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a>, and other countries arrived in the mid-19th century as indentured servants.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>  After the ending of the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_slave_trade" title="Atlantic slave trade">Atlantic slave trade</a>, the population increased naturally.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> The total regional population was estimated at 37.5 million by 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-p2000_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p2000-57">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haiti</a> and most of the <a href="/wiki/French_Caribbean" class="mw-redirect" title="French Caribbean">French</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anglophone_Caribbean" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglophone Caribbean">Anglophone</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dutch_West_Indies" class="mw-redirect" title="Dutch West Indies">Dutch Caribbean</a>, the population is predominantly of <a href="/wiki/Afro-Caribbean" title="Afro-Caribbean">African</a> origin; on many islands there are also significant populations of mixed racial origin (including <a href="/wiki/Mulatto" title="Mulatto">Mulatto</a>-<a href="/wiki/Creole_peoples" title="Creole peoples">Creole</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dougla" title="Dougla">Dougla</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mestizo" title="Mestizo">Mestizo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Quadroon" title="Quadroon">Quadroon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cholo" title="Cholo">Cholo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Castizo" title="Castizo">Castizo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Criollo_people" title="Criollo people">Criollo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zambo" title="Zambo">Zambo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pardo" title="Pardo">Pardo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Asian_Latin_Americans" title="Asian Latin Americans">Asian Latin Americans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chindian" title="Chindian">Chindian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cocoa_panyols" title="Cocoa panyols">Cocoa panyols</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_(mixed_ancestry)" title="Eurasian (mixed ancestry)">Eurasian</a>), as well as populations of European ancestry:  <a href="/wiki/Dutch_people" title="Dutch people">Dutch</a>, <a href="/wiki/English_people" title="English people">English</a>, <a href="/wiki/French_people" title="French people">French</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Italian people">Italian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_people" title="Portuguese people">Portuguese</a> and <a href="/wiki/Spanish_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Spanish people">Spanish</a> ancestry. <a href="/wiki/Asians" class="mw-redirect" title="Asians">Asians</a>, especially those of <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Caribbean" class="mw-redirect" title="Chinese Caribbean">Chinese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indo-Caribbean" class="mw-redirect" title="Indo-Caribbean">Indian</a> descent, and <a href="/wiki/Javanese_people" title="Javanese people">Javanese</a> <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Indonesian people">Indonesians</a>, form a significant minority in parts of the region. <a href="/wiki/Indo-Caribbean" class="mw-redirect" title="Indo-Caribbean">Indians</a> form a plurality of the population in <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Trinidad and Tobago">Trinidad and Tobago</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guyana" title="Guyana">Guyana</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Suriname" title="Suriname">Suriname</a>. Most of their ancestors arrived in the 19th century as indentured laborers.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Caribbean" class="mw-redirect" title="Spanish Caribbean">Spanish-speaking Caribbean</a> populations are primarily of <a href="/wiki/White_Latin_American" class="mw-redirect" title="White Latin American">European</a>, African, or racially mixed origins. Puerto Rico has a European majority with a mixture of European-African-Native American (tri-racial), and a large Mulatto (European-West African) and West African minority. Cuba also has a European majority, along with a significant population of African ancestry. The Dominican Republic has the largest mixed-race population, primarily descended from Europeans, <a href="/wiki/West_African" class="mw-redirect" title="West African">West Africans</a>, and Amerindians.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Revellers_Wine_at_Trinidad_Carnival.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Revellers_Wine_at_Trinidad_Carnival.jpg/220px-Revellers_Wine_at_Trinidad_Carnival.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Revellers_Wine_at_Trinidad_Carnival.jpg/330px-Revellers_Wine_at_Trinidad_Carnival.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Revellers_Wine_at_Trinidad_Carnival.jpg/440px-Revellers_Wine_at_Trinidad_Carnival.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="800" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Revellers_Wine_at_Trinidad_Carnival.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Carnival in Trinidad and Tobago</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">Jamaica</a> has a large African majority, in addition to a significant population of mixed racial background, and has minorities of <a href="/wiki/Chinese_people" title="Chinese people">Chinese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Europeans" class="mw-redirect" title="Europeans">Europeans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indian_people" title="Indian people">Indians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Latino" title="Latino">Latinos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">Jews</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Arab" class="mw-redirect" title="Arab">Arabs</a>. This is a result of years of importation of slaves and indentured laborers, and migration. Most multi-racial Jamaicans refer to themselves as either mixed race or brown. Similar populations can be found in the <a href="/wiki/Caricom" class="mw-redirect" title="Caricom">Caricom</a> states of <a href="/wiki/Belize" title="Belize">Belize</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guyana" title="Guyana">Guyana</a> and <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Trinidad and Tobago">Trinidad and Tobago</a>. <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Trinidad and Tobago">Trinidad and Tobago</a> has a multi-racial cosmopolitan society due to the arrivals of <a href="/wiki/Afro-Trinidadian" class="mw-redirect" title="Afro-Trinidadian">Africans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indo-Trinidadian" class="mw-redirect" title="Indo-Trinidadian">Indians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Trinidadian" class="mw-redirect" title="Chinese Trinidadian">Chinese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arabs" title="Arabs">Arabs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">Jews</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spanish_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Spanish people">Spanish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_people" title="Portuguese people">Portuguese</a>, and <a href="/wiki/White_Trinidadian" class="mw-redirect" title="White Trinidadian">Europeans</a> along with the <a href="/wiki/Amerindians" class="mw-redirect" title="Amerindians">Native Amerindians</a> population. This multi-racial mix has created sub-ethnicities that often straddle the boundaries of major ethnicities and include <a href="/wiki/Dougla" title="Dougla">Dougla</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chindian" title="Chindian">Chindian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mulatto" title="Mulatto">Mulatto</a>-<a href="/wiki/Creole_peoples" title="Creole peoples">Creole</a>, <a href="/wiki/Afro-Asians" title="Afro-Asians">Afro-Asians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_(mixed_ancestry)" title="Eurasian (mixed ancestry)">Eurasian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cocoa_panyols" title="Cocoa panyols">Cocoa panyols</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Asian_Latin_Americans" title="Asian Latin Americans">Asian Latin Americans</a>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Language">Language</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caribbean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Language">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_the_Caribbean" title="Languages of the Caribbean">Languages of the Caribbean</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Spanish" title="Caribbean Spanish">Spanish</a> (64%),  <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a> (25%), <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_English" title="Caribbean English">English</a> (14%), <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Haitian_Creole" title="Haitian Creole">Haitian Creole</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Papiamento" title="Papiamento">Papiamento</a> are the predominant official languages of various countries in the region, although a handful of unique <a href="/wiki/Creole_language" title="Creole language">creole languages</a> or dialects can also be found in virtually every Caribbean country. Other languages such as <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Hindustani" title="Caribbean Hindustani">Caribbean Hindustani</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chinese_language" title="Chinese language">Chinese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_language" title="Indonesian language">Indonesian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_languages_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous languages of the Americas">Amerindian languages</a>, other <a href="/wiki/African_languages" class="mw-redirect" title="African languages">African languages</a>, other <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Europe" title="Languages of Europe">European languages</a>, other <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_India" title="Languages of India">Indian languages</a>, and other <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Indonesia" title="Languages of Indonesia">Indonesian languages</a> can also be found.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caribbean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
