<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Haitian_vodou_altar_to_Petwo,_Rada,_and_Gede_spirits;_November_5,_2010..jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Haitian_vodou_altar_to_Petwo%2C_Rada%2C_and_Gede_spirits%3B_November_5%2C_2010..jpg/220px-Haitian_vodou_altar_to_Petwo%2C_Rada%2C_and_Gede_spirits%3B_November_5%2C_2010..jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Haitian_vodou_altar_to_Petwo%2C_Rada%2C_and_Gede_spirits%3B_November_5%2C_2010..jpg/330px-Haitian_vodou_altar_to_Petwo%2C_Rada%2C_and_Gede_spirits%3B_November_5%2C_2010..jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Haitian_vodou_altar_to_Petwo%2C_Rada%2C_and_Gede_spirits%3B_November_5%2C_2010..jpg/440px-Haitian_vodou_altar_to_Petwo%2C_Rada%2C_and_Gede_spirits%3B_November_5%2C_2010..jpg 2x" data-file-width="3640" data-file-height="2476" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Haitian_vodou_altar_to_Petwo,_Rada,_and_Gede_spirits;_November_5,_2010..jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Haitian_Vodou" title="Haitian Vodou">Haitian Vodou</a> alter</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> is the predominant religion in the Caribbean (84.7%).<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> Other religious groups in the region are <a href="/wiki/Hinduism_in_the_West_Indies" title="Hinduism in the West Indies">Hinduism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">Judaism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rastafarianism" class="mw-redirect" title="Rastafarianism">Rastafarianism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chinese_folk_religion" title="Chinese folk religion">Chinese folk religion</a> (<a href="/wiki/Taoism" title="Taoism">Taoism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Confucianism" title="Confucianism">Confucianism</a>), <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD" class="mw-redirect" title="Bahá&#39;í">Bahá'í</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jainism" title="Jainism">Jainism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sikhism" title="Sikhism">Sikhism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zorastrianism" class="mw-redirect" title="Zorastrianism">Zorastrianism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kebatinan" class="mw-redirect" title="Kebatinan">Kebatinan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Traditional_African_religions" title="Traditional African religions">Traditional African religions</a>, <a href="/wiki/Afro-American_religions" class="mw-redirect" title="Afro-American religions">Afro-American religions</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yoruba_religion" title="Yoruba religion">Yoruba</a> (<a href="/wiki/Santer%C3%ADa" title="Santería">Santería</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_Orisha" title="Trinidad Orisha">Trinidad Orisha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Palo_(religion)" title="Palo (religion)">Palo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Umbanda" title="Umbanda">Umbanda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brujer%C3%ADa" title="Brujería">Brujería</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hoodoo_(folk_magic)" title="Hoodoo (folk magic)">Hoodoo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Candombl%C3%A9" title="Candomblé">Candomblé</a>, <a href="/wiki/Quimbanda" title="Quimbanda">Quimbanda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Orisha" title="Orisha">Orisha</a>, Xangô de Recife, Xangô do Nordeste, Comfa, <a href="/wiki/Espiritismo" title="Espiritismo">Espiritismo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Santo_Daime" title="Santo Daime">Santo Daime</a>, <a href="/wiki/Obeah" title="Obeah">Obeah</a>, <a href="/wiki/Candombl%C3%A9" title="Candomblé">Candomblé</a>, <a href="/wiki/Abaku%C3%A1" title="Abakuá">Abakuá</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kumina" title="Kumina">Kumina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Winti" title="Winti">Winti</a>, Sanse, <a href="/wiki/Cuban_Vod%C3%BA" title="Cuban Vodú">Cuban Vodú</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Vud%C3%BA" title="Dominican Vudú">Dominican Vudú</a>, <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_Voodoo" title="Louisiana Voodoo">Louisiana Voodoo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Haitian_Vodou" title="Haitian Vodou">Haitian Vodou</a>, and <a href="/wiki/West_African_Vodun" title="West African Vodun">Vodun</a>).
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caribbean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Regionalism">Regionalism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caribbean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Regionalism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_CARICOM.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Flag_of_CARICOM.svg/220px-Flag_of_CARICOM.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Flag_of_CARICOM.svg/330px-Flag_of_CARICOM.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Flag_of_CARICOM.svg/440px-Flag_of_CARICOM.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_CARICOM.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Flag of the Caribbean Common Market and Community (CARICOM)</div></div></div>
<p>Caribbean societies are very different from other Western societies in terms of size, culture, and degree of mobility of their citizens.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> The current economic and political problems the states face individually are common to all Caribbean states. Regional development has contributed to attempts to subdue current problems and avoid projected problems. From a political and economic perspective, <a href="/wiki/Regionalism_(international_relations)" title="Regionalism (international relations)">regionalism</a> serves to make Caribbean states active participants in current international affairs through collective coalitions. In 1973, the first political regionalism in the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Basin" title="Caribbean Basin">Caribbean Basin</a> was created by advances of the English-speaking Caribbean nations through the institution known as the Caribbean Common Market and Community (<a href="/wiki/CARICOM" class="mw-redirect" title="CARICOM">CARICOM</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> which is located in Guyana.
</p><p>Certain scholars have argued both for and against generalizing the political structures of the Caribbean. On the one hand the Caribbean states are politically diverse, ranging from communist systems such as Cuba toward more capitalist Westminster-style parliamentary systems as in the Commonwealth Caribbean. Other scholars argue that these differences are superficial, and that they tend to undermine commonalities in the various Caribbean states. Contemporary Caribbean systems seem to reflect a "blending of traditional and modern patterns, yielding hybrid systems that exhibit significant structural variations and divergent constitutional traditions yet ultimately appear to function in similar ways."<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> The political systems of the Caribbean states share similar practices.
</p><p>The influence of regionalism in the Caribbean is often marginalized. Some scholars believe that regionalism cannot exist in the Caribbean because each small state is unique. On the other hand, scholars also suggest that there are commonalities amongst the Caribbean nations that suggest regionalism exists.  "Proximity as well as historical ties among the Caribbean nations has led to cooperation as well as a desire for collective action."<sup id="cite_ref-serbin_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-serbin-62">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> These attempts at regionalization reflect the nations' desires to compete in the international economic system.<sup id="cite_ref-serbin_62-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-serbin-62">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Furthermore, a lack of interest from other major states promoted regionalism in the region.  In recent years the Caribbean has suffered from a lack of U.S. interest. "With the end of the Cold War, U.S. security and economic interests have been focused on other areas. As a result there has been a significant reduction in U.S. aid and investment to the Caribbean."<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>  The lack of international support for these small, relatively poor states, helped regionalism prosper.
</p><p>Following the Cold War another issue of importance in the Caribbean has been the reduced economic growth of some Caribbean States due to the United States and <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>'s allegations of special treatment toward the region by each other.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (December 2011)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States-EU_trade_dispute">United States-EU trade dispute</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caribbean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: United States-EU trade dispute">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The United States under President <a href="/wiki/Bill_Clinton" title="Bill Clinton">Bill Clinton</a> launched a challenge in the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">World Trade Organization</a> against the EU over Europe's preferential program, known as the <a href="/wiki/Lom%C3%A9_Convention" title="Lomé Convention">Lomé Convention</a>, which allowed <a href="/wiki/Banana" title="Banana">banana</a> exports from the former colonies of the <a href="/wiki/ACP_countries" class="mw-redirect" title="ACP countries">Group of African, Caribbean and Pacific states</a> (ACP) to enter Europe cheaply.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> The World Trade Organization sided in the United States' favour and the beneficial elements of the convention to African, Caribbean and Pacific states has been partially dismantled and replaced by the <a href="/wiki/Cotonou_Agreement" title="Cotonou Agreement">Cotonou Agreement</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>During the US/EU dispute, the United States imposed large tariffs on European Union goods (up to 100%) to pressure Europe to change the agreement with the Caribbean nations in favour of the Cotonou Agreement.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Farmers in the Caribbean have complained of falling profits and rising costs as the Lomé Convention weakens.  Some farmers have faced increased pressure to turn towards the cultivation of illegal drugs, which has a higher profit margin and fills the sizable demand for these illegal drugs in North America and Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Caribbean_Financial_Action_Task_Force_and_Association_of_Caribbean_States">Caribbean Financial Action Task Force and Association of Caribbean States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caribbean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Caribbean Financial Action Task Force and Association of Caribbean States">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Caribbean nations have also started to more closely cooperate in the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Financial_Action_Task_Force" title="Caribbean Financial Action Task Force">Caribbean Financial Action Task Force</a> and other instruments to add oversight of the offshore industry. One of the most important associations that deal with regionalism amongst the nations of the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Basin" title="Caribbean Basin">Caribbean Basin</a> has been the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Caribbean_States" title="Association of Caribbean States">Association of Caribbean States</a> (ACS). Proposed by CARICOM in 1992, the ACS soon won the support of the other countries of the region.  It was founded in July 1994.  The ACS maintains regionalism within the Caribbean on issues unique to the Caribbean Basin. Through coalition building, like the ACS and CARICOM, regionalism has become an undeniable part of the politics and economics of the Caribbean.  The successes of region-building initiatives are still debated by scholars, yet regionalism remains prevalent throughout the Caribbean.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Bolivarian_Alliance">Bolivarian Alliance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caribbean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Bolivarian Alliance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The President of <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hugo_Chavez" class="mw-redirect" title="Hugo Chavez">Hugo Chavez</a> launched an economic group called the <a href="/wiki/Bolivarian_Alliance_for_the_Americas" class="mw-redirect" title="Bolivarian Alliance for the Americas">Bolivarian Alliance for the Americas</a> (ALBA), which several eastern Caribbean islands joined.  In 2012, the nation of Haiti, with 9 million people, became the largest CARICOM nation that sought to join the union.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Regional_institutions">Regional institutions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caribbean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Regional institutions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Here are some of the bodies that several islands share in collaboration:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/African,_Caribbean_and_Pacific_Group_of_States" title="African, Caribbean and Pacific Group of States">African, Caribbean and Pacific Group of States</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Association_of_Caribbean_States" title="Association of Caribbean States">Association of Caribbean States</a> (ACS), Trinidad and Tobago</li>
<li>Caribbean Association of Industry and Commerce (CAIC), Trinidad and Tobago</li>
<li>Caribbean Association of National Telecommunication Organizations (CANTO), Trinidad and Tobago<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Community" title="Caribbean Community">Caribbean Community</a> (CARICOM), Guyana</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Development_Bank" title="Caribbean Development Bank">Caribbean Development Bank</a> (CDB), Barbados</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Disaster_Emergency_Management_Agency" title="Caribbean Disaster Emergency Management Agency">Caribbean Disaster Emergency Management Agency</a> (CDERA), Barbados</li>
<li>Caribbean Educators Network<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Caribbean Electric Utility Services Corporation (CARILEC), Saint Lucia<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Examinations_Council" title="Caribbean Examinations Council">Caribbean Examinations Council</a> (CXC), Barbados and Jamaica</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Financial_Action_Task_Force" title="Caribbean Financial Action Task Force">Caribbean Financial Action Task Force</a> (CFATF), Trinidad and Tobago</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Food_Crops_Society" title="Caribbean Food Crops Society">Caribbean Food Crops Society</a>, Puerto Rico</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Football_Union" title="Caribbean Football Union">Caribbean Football Union</a> (CFU), Jamaica</li>
<li>Caribbean Hotel &amp; Tourism Association (CHTA), Florida and Puerto Rico<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Initiative" title="Caribbean Initiative">Caribbean Initiative</a> (Initiative of the IUCN)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Programme_for_Economic_Competitiveness" title="Caribbean Programme for Economic Competitiveness">Caribbean Programme for Economic Competitiveness</a> (CPEC), Saint Lucia</li>
<li>Caribbean Regional Environmental Programme (CREP), Barbados<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Caribbean Regional Fisheries Mechanism (CRFM), Belize<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Caribbean Regional Negotiating Machinery (CRNM), Barbados and Dominican Republic<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caribbean_Telecommunications_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Caribbean Telecommunications Union (page does not exist)">Caribbean Telecommunications Union</a> (CTU), Trinidad and Tobago</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Tourism_Organization" title="Caribbean Tourism Organization">Caribbean Tourism Organization</a> (CTO), Barbados</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Community_of_Latin_American_and_Caribbean_States" title="Community of Latin American and Caribbean States">Community of Latin American and Caribbean States</a> (CELAC)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Foundation_for_the_Development_of_Caribbean_Children" title="Foundation for the Development of Caribbean Children">Foundation for the Development of Caribbean Children</a>, Barbados</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Latin_America_and_Caribbean_Network_Information_Centre" title="Latin America and Caribbean Network Information Centre">Latin America and Caribbean Network Information Centre</a> (LACNIC), Brazil and <a href="/wiki/Uruguay" title="Uruguay">Uruguay</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Latin_American_Economic_System" title="Latin American Economic System">Latin American and the Caribbean Economic System</a>, Venezuela</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_Eastern_Caribbean_States" title="Organisation of Eastern Caribbean States">Organisation of Eastern Caribbean States</a> (OECS), Saint Lucia</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Economic_Commission_for_Latin_America_and_the_Caribbean" title="United Nations Economic Commission for Latin America and the Caribbean">United Nations Economic Commission for Latin America and the Caribbean</a> (ECLAC), <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chile</a> and Trinidad and Tobago</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_the_West_Indies" title="University of the West Indies">University of the West Indies</a>, Jamaica, Barbados, Trinidad and Tobago.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>  In addition, the fourth campus, the Open Campus was formed in June 2008 as a result of an amalgamation of the Board for Non-Campus Countries and Distance Education, Schools of Continuing Studies, the UWI Distance Education Centres and Tertiary Level Units.  The Open Campus has 42 physical sites in 16 Anglophone caribbean countries.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/West_Indies_Cricket_Board" class="mw-redirect" title="West Indies Cricket Board">West Indies Cricket Board</a>, Antigua and Barbuda<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caribbean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_cuisine" title="Caribbean cuisine">Caribbean cuisine</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Favorite_or_national_dishes">Favorite or national dishes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caribbean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Favorite or national dishes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Caribbean&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. <div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:FOOD_Doubles_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/FOOD_Doubles_2.jpg/220px-FOOD_Doubles_2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/FOOD_Doubles_2.jpg/330px-FOOD_Doubles_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/FOOD_Doubles_2.jpg/440px-FOOD_Doubles_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4320" data-file-height="3240" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:FOOD_Doubles_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Doubles_(food)" title="Doubles (food)">Doubles</a>, one of the national dishes of <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Trinidad and Tobago">Trinidad and Tobago</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Arroz_con_gandules.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Arroz_con_gandules.jpg/220px-Arroz_con_gandules.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Arroz_con_gandules.jpg/330px-Arroz_con_gandules.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Arroz_con_gandules.jpg/440px-Arroz_con_gandules.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Arroz_con_gandules.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Arroz_con_gandules" title="Arroz con gandules">Arroz con gandules</a>, one of the national dishes of <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a></div></div></div>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Anguilla" title="Anguilla">Anguilla</a> – rice, peas and fish</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Antigua_and_Barbuda_cuisine" title="Antigua and Barbuda cuisine">Antigua and Barbuda</a> – <a href="/wiki/Fungee" class="mw-redirect" title="Fungee">fungee</a> and <a href="/wiki/Guyana_pepperpot" class="mw-redirect" title="Guyana pepperpot">pepperpot</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bahamas" class="mw-redirect" title="Bahamas">Bahamas</a> - <a href="/wiki/Guava_duff" class="mw-redirect" title="Guava duff">Guava duff</a>, Conch Salad, Peas n' Rice, and Conch Fritters</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">Barbados</a> – <a href="/wiki/Cou-cou" title="Cou-cou">cou-cou</a> and <a href="/wiki/Flying_fish" title="Flying fish">flying fish</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Belize" title="Belize">Belize</a> - rice and beans, stew chicken with potato salad&#160;; white rice, stew beans and fry fish with cole slaw</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/British_Virgin_Islands" title="British Virgin Islands">British Virgin Islands</a> – fish and <a href="/wiki/Fungee" class="mw-redirect" title="Fungee">fungee</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cayman_Islands" title="Cayman Islands">Cayman Islands</a> – turtle stew, turtle steak, <a href="/wiki/Grouper" title="Grouper">grouper</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Colombian_cuisine" title="Colombian cuisine">Colombian</a> Caribbean – rice with coconut milk, <a href="/wiki/Arroz_con_pollo" title="Arroz con pollo">arroz con pollo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sancocho" title="Sancocho">sancocho</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arab_cuisine" title="Arab cuisine">Arab cuisine</a> (due to the large Arab population)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cuban_cuisine" title="Cuban cuisine">Cuba</a> – <a href="/wiki/Platillo_Moros_y_Cristianos" class="mw-redirect" title="Platillo Moros y Cristianos">platillo Moros y Cristianos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ropa_vieja" title="Ropa vieja">ropa vieja</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lechon" title="Lechon">lechon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Plantain_(cooking)" class="mw-redirect" title="Plantain (cooking)">maduros</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ajiaco" title="Ajiaco">ajiaco</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dominica_cuisine" title="Dominica cuisine">Dominica</a> – <a href="/wiki/Mountain_chicken" class="mw-redirect" title="Mountain chicken">mountain chicken</a>, rice and peas, dumplings, saltfish, dashin, bakes (fried dumplings), coconut confiture, curry goat, cassava <a href="/wiki/Farine" class="mw-redirect" title="Farine">farine</a>, oxtail</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic_cuisine" title="Dominican Republic cuisine">Dominican Republic</a> – <a href="/wiki/Arroz_con_pollo" title="Arroz con pollo">arroz con pollo</a> with stewed red <a href="/wiki/Kidney_bean" title="Kidney bean">kidney beans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pan_fry" class="mw-redirect" title="Pan fry">pan fried</a> or <a href="/wiki/Braised" class="mw-redirect" title="Braised">braised</a> beef, salad/ ensalada de coditos, <a href="/wiki/Empanadas" class="mw-redirect" title="Empanadas">empanadas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mang%C3%BA_(dish)" class="mw-redirect" title="Mangú (dish)">mangú</a>, sancocho</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Grenadan_cuisine" class="mw-redirect" title="Grenadan cuisine">Grenada</a> – <a href="/wiki/Oil_down" title="Oil down">oil down</a>, Roti and rice &amp; chicken</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Guyana" title="Guyana">Guyana</a> – <a href="/wiki/Guyana_pepperpot" class="mw-redirect" title="Guyana pepperpot">pepperpot</a>, cookup rice, <a href="/wiki/Roti" title="Roti">roti</a> and <a href="/wiki/Curry" title="Curry">curry</a>, methem, <a href="/wiki/Pholourie" title="Pholourie">pholourie</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Haitian_cuisine" title="Haitian cuisine">Haiti</a> – griot (fried pork) served with du riz a pois or diri ak pwa (<a href="/wiki/Rice_and_beans" title="Rice and beans">rice and beans</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jamaican_cuisine" title="Jamaican cuisine">Jamaica</a> – <a href="/wiki/Ackee_and_saltfish" title="Ackee and saltfish">ackee and saltfish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Callaloo" title="Callaloo">callaloo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jerk_chicken" class="mw-redirect" title="Jerk chicken">jerk chicken</a>, <a href="/wiki/Curry_chicken" class="mw-redirect" title="Curry chicken">curry chicken</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Montserrat" title="Montserrat">Montserrat</a> – <a href="/wiki/Goat_water" title="Goat water">Goat water</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rican_cuisine" title="Puerto Rican cuisine">Puerto Rico</a> – yellow rice with green <a href="/wiki/Pigeon_pea" title="Pigeon pea">pigeon peas</a>, saltfish stew, roasted pork shoulder, chicken fricassée, mofongo, tripe soup, alcapurria, coconut custard, rice pudding, guava turnovers, Mallorca bread</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis" title="Saint Kitts and Nevis">Saint Kitts and Nevis</a> – <a href="/wiki/Goat_water" title="Goat water">goat water</a>, coconut dumplings, spicy <a href="/wiki/Plantain_(cooking)" class="mw-redirect" title="Plantain (cooking)">plantain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saltfish" class="mw-redirect" title="Saltfish">saltfish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Breadfruit" title="Breadfruit">breadfruit</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Saint_Lucian_cuisine" title="Saint Lucian cuisine">Saint Lucia</a> – <a href="/wiki/Callaloo" title="Callaloo">callaloo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dal" title="Dal">dal</a> <a href="/wiki/Roti" title="Roti">roti</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dried_and_salted_cod" title="Dried and salted cod">dried and salted cod</a>, green <a href="/wiki/Banana" title="Banana">bananas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rice_and_beans" title="Rice and beans">rice and beans</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines" title="Saint Vincent and the Grenadines">Saint Vincent and the Grenadines</a> – roasted <a href="/wiki/Breadfruit" title="Breadfruit">breadfruit</a> and fried jackfish</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Suriname" title="Suriname">Suriname</a> – brown beans and rice, <a href="/wiki/Roti" title="Roti">roti</a> and <a href="/wiki/Curry" title="Curry">curry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peanut_soup" title="Peanut soup">peanut soup</a>, battered <a href="/wiki/Fried_plantain" title="Fried plantain">fried plantain</a> with <a href="/wiki/Peanut_sauce" title="Peanut sauce">peanut sauce</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nasi_goreng" title="Nasi goreng">nasi goreng</a>, moksie alesi, <a href="/wiki/Vada_(food)" title="Vada (food)">bara</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pom_(dish)" title="Pom (dish)">pom</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago_cuisine" title="Trinidad and Tobago cuisine">Trinidad and Tobago</a> – <a href="/wiki/Callaloo" title="Callaloo">callaloo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Doubles_(food)" title="Doubles (food)">doubles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aloo_pie" title="Aloo pie">aloo pie</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pholourie" title="Pholourie">phulourie</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bake_and_Shark" title="Bake and Shark">bake and shark</a>, <a href="/wiki/Curry" title="Curry">curry</a> with <a href="/wiki/Roti" title="Roti">roti</a> or <a href="/wiki/Dal_bhat" title="Dal bhat">dal bhat</a>, curry crab and dumpling</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/United_States_Virgin_Islands" title="United States Virgin Islands">United States Virgin Islands</a> – stewed goat, oxtail or beef, seafood, <a href="/wiki/Callaloo" title="Callaloo">callaloo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cou-cou" title="Cou-cou">fungee</a></li></ul>

<li id="cite_note-8"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-8">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.britannica.com/EBchecked/topic/418612/North-America">"North America"</a>. <i>Britannica Concise Encyclopedia</i>; "...&#160;associated with the continent is Greenland, the largest island in the world, and such offshore groups as the Arctic Archipelago, the <a href="/wiki/Bahamas" class="mw-redirect" title="Bahamas">Bahamas</a>, the Greater and Lesser Antilles, the Queen Charlotte Islands, and the Aleutian Islands," but also "North America is bounded ... on the south by the Caribbean Sea," and "according to some authorities, North America begins not at the Isthmus of Panama but at the narrows of <a href="/wiki/Tehuantepec" title="Tehuantepec">Tehuantepec</a>."</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-9"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-9">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.cia.gov/library/publications/the-world-factbook/geos/xx.html"><i>The World: Geographic Overview</i></a>, The World Factbook, Central Intelligence Agency; "North America is commonly understood to include the island of Greenland, the isles of the Caribbean, and to extend south all the way to the Isthmus of Panama."</span>

United Nations Statistics Division. 2008<span class="reference-accessdate">. </li>
<li id="cite_note-32"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-32">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Since the <a href="/wiki/Lucayan_Archipelago" title="Lucayan Archipelago">Lucayan Archipelago</a> is located in the Atlantic Ocean rather than <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">Caribbean Sea</a>, the <a href="/wiki/The_Bahamas" title="The Bahamas">Bahamas</a> are part of the <a href="/wiki/West_Indies" title="West Indies">West Indies</a> but are not technically part of the Caribbean, although the United Nations groups them with the Caribbean.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-nethant-33"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-nethant_33-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-nethant_33-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-nethant_33-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">Population estimates are taken from the <cite class="citation web">Central Bureau of Statistics Netherlands Antilles. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20100501150627/http://www.cbs.an/population/population_b2.asp">"Statistical information: Population"</a>. Government of the Netherlands Antilles. Archived from <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.cbs.an/population/population_b2.asp">the original</a> on 1 May 2010<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">14 October</span> 2010</span>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Statistical+information%3A+Population&amp;rft.pub=Government+of+the+Netherlands+Antilles&amp;rft.au=Central+Bureau+of+Statistics+Netherlands+Antilles&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.cbs.an%2Fpopulation%2Fpopulation_b2.asp&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ACaribbean" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-34"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-34">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Because of ongoing activity of the <a href="/wiki/Soufriere_Hills_volcano" class="mw-redirect" title="Soufriere Hills volcano">Soufriere Hills volcano</a> beginning in July 1995, much of Plymouth was destroyed and government offices were relocated to Brades. Plymouth remains the <i>de jure</i> capital.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-35"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-35">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Since the <a href="/wiki/Lucayan_Archipelago" title="Lucayan Archipelago">Lucayan Archipelago</a> is located in the Atlantic Ocean rather than <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">Caribbean Sea</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Turks_and_Caicos_Islands" title="Turks and Caicos Islands">Turks and Caicos Islands</a> are part of the <a href="/wiki/West_Indies" title="West Indies">West Indies</a> but are not technically part of the Caribbean, although the United Nations groups them with the Caribbean.</span>
